class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Comparison of text editors</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>This article provides basic comparisons for common <a href="/wiki/Text_editor" title="Text editor">text editors</a>. More feature details for text editors are available from the <i><a href="/wiki/Category:Text_editor_features" title="Category:Text editor features">Category of text editor features</a></i> and from the individual products\' articles. This article may not be up-to-date or necessarily all-inclusive.\n</p><p>Feature comparisons are made between stable versions of software, not the upcoming versions or <i>beta</i> releases \xe2\x80\x93 and are exclusive of any add-ons, extensions or external programs (unless specified in footnotes).\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><b>Multiple instances</b>: multiple instances of the program can be opened simultaneously for editing multiple files. Applies both for <a href="/wiki/Single_document_interface" class="mw-redirect" title="Single document interface">single document interface</a> (SDI) and multiple document interface (MDI) programs. Also applies for program that has a user interface that looks like multiple instances of the same program (such as some versions of <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Word" title="Microsoft Word">Microsoft Word</a>).</li>\n<li><b>Single document window splitting</b>: window can be split to simultaneously view different areas of a file.</li>\n<li><b>MDI: Overlappable windows</b>: each opened document gets its own fully movable window inside the editor environment.</li>\n<li><b>MDI: Tabbed document interface</b>: multiple documents can be viewed as tabs in a single window.</li>\n<li><b>MDI: Window splitting</b>: splitting application window to show multiple documents (non-overlapping windows).</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Basic_features">Basic features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_text_editors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Basic features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align: center; text-align: center;" class="unknown table-unknown">?\n</td>\n<td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes\n</td></tr>\n<tr class="sortbottom">\n<th>\n</th>\n<th>Syntax highlighting\n</th>\n<th>Function list\n</th>\n<th>Symbol database <br />(ctags or equiv.)\n</th>\n<th>Bracket matching\n</th>\n<th>Auto indentation\n</th>\n<th>Auto completion\n</th>\n<th>Code folding\n</th>\n<th>Text folding\n</th>\n<th>Compiler integration\n</th></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes_2">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_text_editors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><b>Syntax highlighting</b>: Displays text in different colors and fonts according to the category of terms.</li>\n<li><b>Function list</b>: Lists all functions from current file in a window or sidebar and allows user to jump directly to the definition of that function for example by double-clicking on the function name in the list. More or less realtime (does not require creating a symbol database, see below).</li>\n<li><b>Symbol database</b>: Database of functions, variable and type definitions, macro definitions etc. in all the files belonging to the software being developed. The database can be created by the editor itself or by an external program such as ctags. The database can be used to instantly locate the definition even if it is in another file.</li>\n<li><b>Bracket matching</b>: Find matching parenthesis or bracket, taking into account nesting.</li>\n<li><b>Auto indentation</b>: May refer to just simple <a href="/wiki/Indentation_(typesetting)" title="Indentation (typesetting)">indenting</a> to the same level as the line above, or intelligent indenting that is language specific, e.g., ensuring a given <a href="/wiki/Indent_style" class="mw-redirect" title="Indent style">indent style</a>.</li>\n<li><b>Compiler integration</b>: Allows running compilers/linkers/debuggers from within editor, capturing the compiler output and stepping through errors, automatically moving cursor to corresponding location in the source file.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Extra_features">Extra features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_text_editors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Extra features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align: center; font-size: 85%; width: auto; table-layout: fixed;">\n<caption>Text editor support for other programming features\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="width: 12em">\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Shell_(computing)#Text_(CLI)_shells" title="Shell (computing)">Text shell</a> integration\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Shell_(computing)#Graphical_(GUI)_shells" title="Shell (computing)">Graphical shell</a> integration\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Macro_(computer_science)" title="Macro (computer science)">Macro language</a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Collaborative_real-time_editor" title="Collaborative real-time editor">Collaborative editing</a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="#ref_lfs">Large file support</a>\n</th>\n<th>Long line support\n</th>\n<th>Multi-line <a href="/wiki/Regular_expression" title="Regular expression">regex</a> support<sup id="cite_ref-multi_line_regex_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multi_line_regex-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th>Search in files\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background: #ececec; font-size: 90%">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes\n</td>\n<td>= Larger than 4&#160;GB (<a href="/wiki/Large_file_support" title="Large file support">LFS</a>)\n</td>\n<td style="background:#bfd; color:black; vertical-align:middle; text-align:center;" class="table-yes2">2 GB\n</td>\n<td>= Larger than 1&#160;GB, not limited by memory\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background: #FFD; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="partial table-partial">memory\n</td>\n<td>= Limited by available memory &#160;&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No (64&#160;KB)\n</td>\n<td>= Some limit less than available memory (give max size if known)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In general, most text editors do not support large text files. Some restrict themselves to available in-core RAM while others use sophisticated virtual memory management techniques and paging algorithms.<sup id="cite_ref-large_text_editors_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-large_text_editors-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Search in files:</b>\nPerform search (and possibly replace) in multiple files on disk, for example on a sub-directory and recursively all the directories below it.\nSimilar to <a href="/wiki/Grep" title="Grep">grep</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Key_bindings">Key bindings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_text_editors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Key bindings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Support for <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_shortcut#Customization" title="Keyboard shortcut">custom key bindings</a>.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align: center; Ctrl-9, Ctrl-0 cannot be set, nor is Control-Shift-&lt;char&gt; distinguished from Ctrl-&lt;char&gt;.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Notepad++: custom shortcuts of Shift-&lt;char&gt; cannot be set, they need an added modifier such as Ctrl or Alt. i.e. SCI_LINESCROLLUP cannot be bound to "Shift-I" as the "Add" button is greyed out.</li>\n<li>Emacs and Pico: pico uses most of Emacs\'s motion and deletion commands: ^F ^B ^P ^N ^D etc.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Protocol_support">Protocol support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_text_editors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Protocol support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Support for editing files over a network or the Internet.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align: center; For UTF-8 and UTF-16, this requires internal 16-bit character support.\n</p><p><b>Partial</b> support is indicated if: 1) the editor can only <i>convert</i> the character encoding to internal (8-bit) format for editing.\n2) If some encodings are supported only in <i>some platforms</i>.\n3) If the editor can only <i>display</i> specific character set (such as OEM) by loading corresponding font, but does not support keyboard entry for that character set.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align: center; text-align: center;" class="unknown table-unknown">?\n</td>\n<td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-XEmacs_Unicode_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XEmacs_Unicode-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background: #ececec; color: black; font-weight: bold; vertical-align: middle; text-align: left;" class="table-rh"><a href="/wiki/Yi_(editor)" title="Yi (editor)">Yi</a>\n</th>\n<td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes\n</td>\n<td style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; font-size: smaller; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="unknown table-unknown">?\n</td>\n<td style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; font-size: smaller; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="unknown table-unknown">?\n</td>\n<td style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; font-size: smaller; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="unknown table-unknown">?\n</td>\n<td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes\n</td>\n<td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No\n</td></tr>\n<tr class="sortbottom">\n<th>\n</th>\n<th>ASCII\n</th>\n<th>ISO-8859\n</th>\n<th>DOS (OEM)\n</th>\n<th>EBCDIC\n</th>\n<th>UTF-8\n</th>\n<th>UTF-16\n</th></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Right-to-left_and_bidirectional_text">Right-to-left and bidirectional text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comparison_of_text_editors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Right-to-left and bidirectional text">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Support for <a href="/wiki/Right-To-Left" class="mw-redirect" title="Right-To-Left">Right-To-Left</a> (RTL) texts is necessary for editing some languages like <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hebrew" class="mw-redirect" title="Hebrew">Hebrew</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yiddish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Yiddish language">Yiddish</a> and the mixture of left to right (LTR) and RTL known as bi-directional (<a href="/wiki/Bi-directional_text" title="Bi-directional text">BiDi</a>) support.\n</p><p>Depending on the algorithm used in the programs it might only render the bidirectional text correctly but may not be able to edit them. (e.g. Notepad++ 5.1.3 shows bidirectional texts correctly but cannot edit it and user should change the text direction to RTL to be able to edit RTL texts correctly.)\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align: center; font-size: 85%; width: auto; table-layout: fixed;">\n<caption>Right to left (RTL) &amp; bidirectional (bidi) support\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="width: buffer\xe2\x80\x99s size cannot be larger than some maximum, which is defined by the largest buffer position representable by Emacs integers. This is because Emacs tracks buffer positions using that data type. For typical 64-bit machines, this maximum buffer size is 2^{61} - 2 bytes, or about 2 EiB. class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Vedit_Unicode_158-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Vedit_Unicode_158-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span Characters not included in Windows charset can be preserved.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-vim_ebcdic-159"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-vim_ebcdic_159-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Vim</i> supports EBCDIC when compiled on a system that uses the EBCDIC character set.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-XEmacs_Unicode-160"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-XEmacs_Unicode_160-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">from version 21.5.29</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-gnuEmacsBidi-161"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-gnuEmacsBidi_161-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>GNU Emacs</i><br /><br /> (1) According to a comment in the source file where the bidi support is implemented (<a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://git.savannah.gnu.org/cgit/emacs.git/tree/src/bidi.c">http://git.savannah.gnu.org/cgit/emacs.git/tree/src/bidi.c</a> accessed August 15, 2017), GNU Emacs doesn\'t fully conform to the Unicode Bidirectional Algorithm (Unicode Annex #9, a.k.a. UAX #9) in the way it wraps the lines of a bidi paragraph: "we are violating paragraph 3.4 of UAX#9. which mandates that line breaking shall be done before reordering each screen line separately." <br /><br />(2) According to the online GNU Emacs manual (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.gnu.org/software/emacs/manual/html_node/emacs/Bidirectional-Editing.html#Bidirectional-Editing">section 22.19 Bidirectional Editing</a>, accessed August 15, 2017), for the purpose of changing paragraph direction, "Paragraph boundaries are empty lines, i.e., lines consisting entirely of whitespace character". This contrasts with the otherwise ubiquitous convention of regarding the newline marker (LF on Unix derivatives, including macOS, and CR+LF on Windows) as the paragraph separator in plain text documents. However starting with version 26.0.50, the bidi paragraph separator can be customized.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-minedBidi-162"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-minedBidi_162-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-minedBidi_162-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>mined</i>: supports bidi in cooperation with bidi terminal (mlterm, mintty); also supports "poor man\'s bidi mode" (automatic visual text order right-to-left input) in normal terminal</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-NotepadppBidi-163"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-NotepadppBidi_163-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Notepadpp</i>: Scintilla (Notepad++\'s Engine) does not really support bidirectional editing. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://sourceforge.net/p/scintilla/bugs/757/#01c9">https://sourceforge.net/p/scintilla/bugs/757/#01c9</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-164"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-164">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://superuser.com/questions/439440/did-mac-os-lion-switch-to-using-line-feeds-lf-n-for-line-breaks-instead-of">"Did Mac OS Lion switch to using line feeds (LF \'\\n\') for line breaks instead of carriage returns (CR \'\\r\')?"</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Did+Mac+OS+Lion+switch+to+using+line+feeds+%28LF+%27%5Cn%27%29+for+line+breaks+instead+of+carriage+returns+%28CR+%27%5Cr%27%29%3F&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fsuperuser.com%2Fquestions%2F439440%2Fdid-mac-os-lion-switch-to-using-line-feeds-lf-n-for-line-breaks-instead-of&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AComparison+of+text+editors" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-gnuEmacsNewline-165"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-gnuEmacsNewline_165-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>GNU Emacs</i>: GNU Emacs doesn\'t regard the newline marker as a paragraph separator in bidi texts.
